  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_036c9f03-8aaf-461f-bd32-f8d6cba5e7a4'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer9629710347147009014"><b>Smart and Spicy, The Children of The Gods Paranormal Romance Series will keep you at the edge of your seat!</b><br/><br/><b>A fascinating blend of Mythology, Cyber-war, and a tender Shades of Grey Romance, <i>Dark Stranger – The Dream</i> captivates the hearts and minds of readers around the world.</b><br/><br/>Since the dawn of human civilization, two warring factions of near-immortals – the descendants of th</span>
  <span id="freeText9629710347147009014" style="display:none"><b>Smart and Spicy, The Children of The Gods Paranormal Romance Series will keep you at the edge of your seat!</b><br /><br /><b>A fascinating blend of Mythology, Cyber-war, and a tender Shades of Grey Romance, <i>Dark Stranger – The Dream</i> captivates the hearts and minds of readers around the world.</b><br /><br />Since the dawn of human civilization, two warring factions of near-immortals – the descendants of the gods of old – have been secretly shaping its destiny. Kian's small clan championing progress, freedom and peace; their powerful enemy propagating ignorance, hate, and war.<br /><br />Leading the clandestine battle from his luxurious L.A. high-rise, Kian is surrounded by family, yet he feels alone. Descending from a single goddess – the only one to survive the ancient cataclysm that wiped out the gods and most of their immortal offspring – clan members are forbidden to each other. And as the only other known immortals are their hated enemies, Kian and his kin have been long resigned to a lonely existence of fleeting trysts with human partners. That is, until Kian's sister Amanda – a researcher of paranormal abilities – makes a game changing discovery; a mortal seeress who she believes is a dormant carrier of their genes. Ever the realist, Kian is skeptical and refuses his sister's plea to attempt the Dormant's activation. But when his enemies learn of the highly coveted soothsayer's existence and attempt to grab her, he rushes her to the safety of his keep. <br /><br />Inexorably drawn to Syssi's shy beauty, Kian is startled by feelings he had sworn off long ago. Tormented by past mistakes, he wrestles with his conscience as he is tempted to explore her budding interest in the spicy passions he favors.<br /><br />When Syssi's paranormal foresight lands her a job at Dr. Amanda Dokani's neuroscience lab, it fails to predict, not only that her boss is an immortal who would drag her into a secret, millennia-old battle over humanity's future, but the professor's imposing brother who would alter her own. <br /><br /><b>Despite his better judgement, will Kian succumb to Syssi's irresistible pull? And will Syssi discover that the man igniting her startlingly dark desires is a nearly two-thousand-year-old immortal?</b><br /><br /><b>Warning.</b> This book contains hot scenes and adult themes. Reader discretion is advised.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9629710347147009014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/959839-i-m-having-a-hard-time-grasping-some-of">I&#39;m having a hard time grasping some of the story points in this series....If Annani had 5 children who were near-immortals and they then had children with mortals - wouldn&#39;t all the children be Dormants? If so, who activated them?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_959839'><a id="like_count_community_question_959839" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/959839?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F26005898-dark-stranger">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/959839-i-m-having-a-hard-time-grasping-some-of">3 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/959839-i-m-having-a-hard-time-grasping-some-of">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/60411370-ksenia"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1480195621i/60411370._UY100_CR6,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/60411370-ksenia">Ksenia</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">You need to reread the explanation of this point in book #1, chapter 45 and book #3, chapter 41. The info just slipped by in there by Kian and Annini.<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You need to reread the explanation of this point in book #1, chapter 45 and book #3, chapter 41. The info just slipped by in there by Kian and Annini.<br /> Annani is the full blooded goddess--the only one who survived the nuclear blast, as far as we know for sure. The rest of immortals are grand-sons of Mortdh--the Doom Brotherhood-- Navuh's sons with dormant females and maybe with other immortal females who survived the original blast in the stronghold. So in the way of immortal power &amp; ability, Kian's counterpart is Navuh, who hides on the island in the Indian ocean. Both were born immortal as 1st generation of gods, not activated with venom. The rest immortals are 3 Annani's daughters Alena, Sari &amp; Amanda, the 2nds son died in battle.<br /><br />As it was explain to us, and as far as I remember it, Annani's children, girls &amp; boys alike, are born immortals without need of venom injection. However Annani's grandchildren are dormant--born mortal and need venom to turn immortal. So she tried the experiment with injecting the blood to her grand-daughter, who was born to her 1st child Alena. After that Annani continued to infuse girls with her blood to facilitate the change. After Kian was mature, he got the boys changed with his venom. And then the boys kept doing it through fight challenge--the different hormones in venom need to change boys to immortal I guess. <br />I hope it helps.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1439281876" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1439281876" />
    <a title="E Varady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7282895-e-varady"><img alt="E Varady" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1439281876?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="E Varady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="E Varady" href="/user/show/7282895-e-varady">E Varady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25835113-dark-stranger">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1439281876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15773417810007480837"><strong>Don't read if you want a strong female lead</strong><br/><br/>If you are like me and like your female leads to be strong and dynamic, don't expect that here. This is a Cinderella story that leaves you wanting a character worthy of the classic storyline. Instead we get a character who is so one dimensional she could be a stick figure. This is a storyline that is all tell and no show, full of awkward backstory and overly detailed descriptions of how everyone looks. Personally, I am more interested in them as complex</span>
  <span id="freeText15773417810007480837" style="display:none"><strong>Don't read if you want a strong female lead</strong><br /><br />If you are like me and like your female leads to be strong and dynamic, don't expect that here. This is a Cinderella story that leaves you wanting a character worthy of the classic storyline. Instead we get a character who is so one dimensional she could be a stick figure. This is a storyline that is all tell and no show, full of awkward backstory and overly detailed descriptions of how everyone looks. Personally, I am more interested in them as complex characters. I can skip the endless chiseled chests/jaw and dainty yet large breasted descriptions, especially when the scenes fall flat emotionally.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15773417810007480837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1410992852" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1410992852" />
    <a title="Celestine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13928747-celestine"><img alt="Celestine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531758529p2/13928747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1410992852?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celestine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celestine" href="/user/show/13928747-celestine">Celestine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13928747-celestine?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1410992852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7723410916298122203">"Dark Stranger The Dream" is the launch of the Children of the Gods series by I.T. Lucas. The author builds her own complicated legendarium based on ancient Sumerian documents and their descriptions of aliens. It is compelling and complicated world-building tied to real-life implications throughout the centuries. In this first installment, Lucas spends considerable time crafting the universe of the near-immortals as the descendants of goddesses. These near-immortals have some of the same physica</span>
  <span id="freeText7723410916298122203" style="display:none">"Dark Stranger The Dream" is the launch of the Children of the Gods series by I.T. Lucas. The author builds her own complicated legendarium based on ancient Sumerian documents and their descriptions of aliens. It is compelling and complicated world-building tied to real-life implications throughout the centuries. In this first installment, Lucas spends considerable time crafting the universe of the near-immortals as the descendants of goddesses. These near-immortals have some of the same physical and mental characteristics ascribed to vampires, such as quick healing, fangs, strength and speed and intensely compelling hyper-sexual manipulation. Two clans of the near-immortals have been at war for centuries and low-birth rates and warfare have reduced numbers to the point that the children of the gods are seeking alternatives to ensure the continuation of their race. One alternative includes seeking mortals with the dormant immortal gene. Dr. Amanda Dokani, sister to the clan regent, believes she has discovered two likely candidates.<br /><br />Syssi's precognition abilities are what first bring her to Amanda's attention, but the two develop a fast friendship. Amanda is sure Syssi may be a solution to the immortals' problems, but Amanda's brother Kian is skeptical. He indulges Amanda's research, but is more consumed by the day-to-day oversight of his large clan, the constant vigilance required to ward off their eternal enemies and marshaling the massive altruistic endeavors his clan sponsors. Then Syssi and Kian meet and the two are inexplicably drawn to one another. Soon afterward, Amanda's research is breached by their enemies and Syssi becomes a target. Without divulging all their immortal secrets, Amanda and Kian have to convince Syssi to come under their protection. <br /><br />The book is told in third person omniscient point of view, with each chapter headed by a name and that person's version of events. At times, the transition is a small overlap of a scene between two characters. This is one of my favorite narrative forms since I appreciate reading a scene from both the hero's and the heroine's point of view. I feel it enriches the story, and Lucas handles it deftly. Several chapters are told from the point of view of minor characters, which adds to the richness of the overall character development and makes the world-building more faceted.<br /><br />This book was a page turner as the "legends" of the immortals expanded and as the intrigue and danger from the enemy clan became more prevalent. Characters have distinct personalities. For instance, Dr. Amanda is brilliant, but a sultry and unapologetic femme fatale. Kian is a product of his ancient oligarchical leadership and is still having trouble adjusting to a more collaborative effort required in a digital age where the clan is spread all over the world. Syssi is shy and quiet, and probably the least fully developed main character, but I have hopes for her coming into her own in future installments.<br /><br />This book does not have a resolved ending, and in fact the author does not promise one until the third book. Luckily all three are already available and offered on Kindle Unlimited. <br /><br />This trilogy reminds me a little of the Krinar Chronicles by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6550220.Anna_Zaires" title="Anna Zaires" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna Zaires</a>. If you enjoyed those books, I think you will have a blast with these.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7723410916298122203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10433033570021410567">Dear Goodreads, never, ever again recomend me a book like this again. It pains me that so many women gave it so many stars (I didn't even want to give it one, I would give it minus five, though). The female characters have the personality of a hair pin. Kian treats Sissy like a dumb child who has to be protected and taken care of and whatever. "Shh, baby, I'm here, you don't have to worry about anything, I'll take care of you, I'll provide." Give me a fucking break. And she's like a real lady bu</span>
  <span id="freeText10433033570021410567" style="display:none">Dear Goodreads, never, ever again recomend me a book like this again. It pains me that so many women gave it so many stars (I didn't even want to give it one, I would give it minus five, though). The female characters have the personality of a hair pin. Kian treats Sissy like a dumb child who has to be protected and taken care of and whatever. "Shh, baby, I'm here, you don't have to worry about anything, I'll take care of you, I'll provide." Give me a fucking break. And she's like a real lady but all his previous lovers weren't, of course. And she's his. For real. And they want to fuck but oh, wait, it's more than that because they met yesterday but they truly care about each other and they feel this connection and... Call me a feminist (please) but this book offended the shit out of me. I'm tired of women to be portrayed as stupid dumbasses waiting for the male to decide their fate. Cavemen need to stop writing romance books, or we have to stop reading them. I really regret reading this one.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13290554804862493472">I am having horrible luck with finding anything Dark. I took the dang title at face value and thought dark romance; it wasn't. It was more of a frustrating romance, but it is a good thing I love those kinds of novels as well. <br/><br/>Kian is a near-immortal. I love that Lucas categories them like this, they can die, but it is tough to do so.   <span id="freeText13290554804862493472" style="display:none">I am having horrible luck with finding anything Dark. I took the dang title at face value and thought dark romance; it wasn't. It was more of a frustrating romance, but it is a good thing I love those kinds of novels as well. <br /><br />Kian is a near-immortal. I love that Lucas categories them like this, they can die, but it is tough to do so. "Everything can die if you drop a nuclear bomb on them" Love that line. <br /><br />So this is a trilogy with a series wrap around. I don't know if that makes sense, but that is what it is. These three deal with Kian and Syssi and then there will be another three that deal with a different set of characters. I will be finishing up with Kian and Syssi and then go from there. It feels like it wants to be like JRWard BDB but to be honest; it's a little more fluffy than that. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16970309645891808350"><b> Holy Sh*t this was awful</b><br/><br/>This book takes you on a long unwinding journey to nowhere! It really doesn't go anywhere. Not to mention, half the book is spent with her dreaming of having sex with the H. <br/><br/>Run for the hills on this one,because if you are looking for a plot line or anything of substance then you won't find it here. Thank God it was free *Shudders*</span>

  <span id="freeText1909275030221571003" style="display:none">DNF at like...I dunno, 25%? 30%? Who even knows because nothing happens? <br /><br />This is like a cut rate first draft of a Black Dagger Brotherhood fanfic, mixed with some Fifty Shades and sprinkled with shit every nerdy 8th grade girl wrote about vampires in study hall back in 1997. <br /><br />If you’re playing bad book bingo this will fill your card fast. Let’s see:<br /><br />- Multiple POVs for no reason<br /><br />- One dimensional heroine who talks up being a strong woman yet seems to have no redeeming value and the core of her personality is her lust for a dominant man<br /><br />- Telling the reader everything instead of letting them figure it out, including the classic “injecting awkward explanations into dialogue purely to tell the reader something”<br /><br />- Mind numbing repetition of physical feature descriptions <br /><br />- Flimsy plot involving villains called “Doomers”<br /><br />- A Mary Sue sister character who is incredibly beautiful, a genius, drives a Porsche<br /><br />- An unlikable hero who reads like an older woman with a conservative streak (instead of the hot alpha male type he is supposed to be)<br /><br />So yeah. This has gotta be a no for me, dawg.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1387967779" />
    <a title="Kerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46065609-kerry"><img alt="Kerry" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1387967779?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1387967779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10484415340576888671">I really enjoyed this book! I've gotten into the paranormal romance genre lately and have really enjoyed it. I have found that some authors succeed at it more than others. I.T. Lucas is very talented and I really liked her usage of science in the book. When I read the description, I was a little worried that the science themes would be over my head, but she really explained them in a way that made it easy to understand. The science was really an added bonus to an already hot novel! I liked the c</span>
  <span id="freeText10484415340576888671" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book! I've gotten into the paranormal romance genre lately and have really enjoyed it. I have found that some authors succeed at it more than others. I.T. Lucas is very talented and I really liked her usage of science in the book. When I read the description, I was a little worried that the science themes would be over my head, but she really explained them in a way that made it easy to understand. The science was really an added bonus to an already hot novel! I liked the characters and thought that they were well developed. I also liked the hot scenes! I'm very hooked on this series already and can't wait to read book 2! I'm sure that it will be just as exciting as this one!</span>

<div id="review_1435049146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1435049146" />
    <a title="Carly Hall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48650749-carly-hall"><img alt="Carly Hall" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1435049146?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carly Hall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carly Hall" href="/user/show/48650749-carly-hall">Carly Hall</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1435049146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17399867143255100651">A branch of a Scottish clan of near immortal makes Los Angeles its home, where its exceptionally good looking members can blend among the many wannabe actors and musicians who flock to the city of lights. Kian, their leader, believes that by hiding in plain sight among the large city's mortal population his people are safe from their enemies the Doomers. Both groups originate from the mythological gods and had been at war since antiquity, when the God Mordth, the God the Doomers worship, had bee</span>
  <span id="freeText17399867143255100651" style="display:none">A branch of a Scottish clan of near immortal makes Los Angeles its home, where its exceptionally good looking members can blend among the many wannabe actors and musicians who flock to the city of lights. Kian, their leader, believes that by hiding in plain sight among the large city's mortal population his people are safe from their enemies the Doomers. Both groups originate from the mythological gods and had been at war since antiquity, when the God Mordth, the God the Doomers worship, had been spurned by the goddess Annani, the matriarch of Kian's clan. He had sworn himself as well as his descendants to wipe out Annani together with her descendants, and to obliterate the gods' matriarchal tradition of a woman's right to choose her mate. The Doomers adhere to his hateful patriarchal legacy, and to keep human society at large from achieving democracy and enlightenment they manipulate global affairs and instigate wars.<br /><br />But the Doomers are not the only problem Kian's clan faces. Annani's descendants can't find immortals who descent from other goddesses to enrich their limited genetic (godly) pool. While Kian is leading the war, his sister Amanda who is a professor of neuroscience is leading a search for Dormants by testing mortals for paranormal abilities. Dormants are carriers of the godly unrealized genes who can be turned into immortals. Her research assistant Syssi's precognition ability is the strongest yet, but to activate Syssi Amanda needs Kian's help. When the Doomers get their hands on Amanda's research material and find about Syssi the story takes off on a page turning thrill ride.<br />Each character has a unique voice and a fully developed personality, and the world building is incredible, with a complete culture and mythology going back to the time of the gods. I loved the deep friendship that develops between Sissy and Amanda despite how different from each other they are in almost every possible way, and how much both Amanda and Kian care about Syssi. The heart-pounding action and Sissy and Kian's titillating romance kept me reading into the night, while the funny scenes woven in between made me laugh out loud.<br />By the time I finished book one I was completely immersed in the story, and by book four I was dreaming about it. The children of the gods is my new favorite urban fantasy series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17399867143255100651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1512694214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1512694214" />
    <a title="Ellie Melili" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51377320-ellie-melili"><img alt="Ellie Melili" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1512694214?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellie Melili" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellie Melili" href="/user/show/51377320-ellie-melili">Ellie Melili</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25835113-dark-stranger">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1512694214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1765289533390801012">Dark Stranger The Dream is a thrilling first book in The Children of The Gods series, and I can tell that this series is going to be amazing. One of those that I grab a book as soon as a new one is out.<br/>Kian is the immortal son of the last surviving goddess and the leader of his clan in the US. He is gruff, short tempered, and the ultimate dominant alpha, but he is also selfless, honorable, totally devoted to his family, and a total hunk. Syssi is smart, shy and soft spoken, but hides a steel bac</span>
  <span id="freeText1765289533390801012" style="display:none">Dark Stranger The Dream is a thrilling first book in The Children of The Gods series, and I can tell that this series is going to be amazing. One of those that I grab a book as soon as a new one is out.<br />Kian is the immortal son of the last surviving goddess and the leader of his clan in the US. He is gruff, short tempered, and the ultimate dominant alpha, but he is also selfless, honorable, totally devoted to his family, and a total hunk. Syssi is smart, shy and soft spoken, but hides a steel backbone. Working in a neuroscience lab, Syssi doesn't know that her boss, Dr. Amanda Dokani (who is Kian's sister), is an immortal and is testing people with paranormal abilities to find humans who are dormant carriers of immortal genes. Amanda suspects that Syssi is a dormant and wants Kian to attempt her activation. He refuses because he finds seducing and deceiving Syssi dishonorable. But when Kian meets Syssi at his sister's lab, his resistance falters, especially since he is forced to spend time with her while rescuing her and Amanda from his enemies the Doomers. Nevertheless, he tries to do the right thing and stay away from Syssi. Syssi feels powerful attraction to Amanda's gorgeous brother, but is intimidated by him and his behavior is confusing her. Syssi thinks he is way out of her league.<br />This was such an exciting read, and not only because of the hot romance. It was fast paced and suspenseful, and the characters read like real people with real problems. I loved both Kian and Syssi, as well as the rest of the cast, and can't wait to find out what happens to them in the next book in the series – Dark Stranger Revealed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1765289533390801012" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Just like that, Kian is whining about how being seperated from her feels wrong (and the author never really explains why that's a necessity) after he has spent a total of maybe 90 non-communicative minutes with her in his whole c</span>
  <span id="freeText1638239615290704149" style="display:none">Very slow start, way too many points of view and not enough detail. Not enough world building happening. Kian and Sissy are ridiculous. They meet say almost literally two words to each other, Sissy falls asleep on Kian in a five minute car ride and bam! They're in love. Just like that, Kian is whining about how being seperated from her feels wrong (and the author never really explains why that's a necessity) after he has spent a total of maybe 90 non-communicative minutes with her in his whole centuries long life. Really? I give up.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8560000558203116193">I don't understand the high ratings for this book. The idea of the story was good; however, the author killed it for me by the constant droning of explanations and inner thoughts. To me the droning was just to fill pages but in doing so I had a very hard time finishing this book. It took me several days because I had to keep putting it down because I was bored. Even the sex was boring. I won't purchase any more from this author. I was disappointed with the author and the people who rated this so</span>
  <span id="freeText8560000558203116193" style="display:none">I don't understand the high ratings for this book. To me the droning was just to fill pages but in doing so I had a very hard time finishing this book. It took me several days because I had to keep putting it down because I was bored. Even the sex was boring. I won't purchase any more from this author. I was disappointed with the author and the people who rated this so highly. P.S., if there was an editor, he/she missed a lot.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6toIx5nF2TOOn6DxaYWFbt0nPzEBTU4fWwoVukn6pK6qbsMamASq0AAKcFIT4e5t2oFEFszK9EuX1J8/Nlt5AQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lsojKpDrDcKy8QfSiHY6lKbsGTruQLDgplaSS3hpkYnWfuj3kSp+ITxk13HyElGXoUpiHSPHCrRqiBjOB8hMJg==')})
  }
